               <td class="sidebar-content"> 
                <ul>
                 <li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">International Men's Day</a></li>
                </ul></td>

        <tr>
         <td class="sidebar-navbar"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r992953826">.mw-parser-output .navbar{display:inline;font-size:88%;font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .navbar-collapse{float:left;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .navbar-boxtext{word-spacing:0}.mw-parser-output .navbar ul{display:inline-block;white-space:nowrap;line-height:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::before{margin-right:-0.125em;content:"[ "}.mw-parser-output .navbar-brackets::after{margin-left:-0.125em;content:" ]"}.mw-parser-output .navbar li{word-spacing:-0.125em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-mini abbr{font-variant:small-caps;border-bottom:none;text-decoration:none;cursor:inherit}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-full{font-size:114%;margin:0 7em}.mw-parser-output .navbar-ct-mini{font-size:114%;margin:0 4em}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox .navbar{display:block;font-size:100%}.mw-parser-output .navbox-title .navbar{float:left;text-align:left;margin-right:0.5em}</style>
          <div class="navbar plainlinks hlist navbar-mini">
           <ul>
            <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Masculism_sidebar" title="Template:Masculism sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Masculism_sidebar" title="Template talk:Masculism sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
            <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Masculism_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
           </ul>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p><b>International Men's Day</b> (<b>IMD</b>) is a global holiday celebrated annually on November 19 to recognize and celebrate the cultural, political, and socioeconomic achievements of men. The objectives of celebrating an International Men's Day are set out in 'All The Six Pillars of International Men's Day'.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-1">[1]</a></sup> It is an occasion to celebrate boys' and men's achievements and contributions, in particular for their contributions to <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">nation</a>, union, <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Community" title="Community">community</a>, <a href="/wiki/Family" title="Family">family</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_care" title="Child care">childcare</a>. The broader and ultimate aim of the event is to promote basic <a href="/wiki/Humanitarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Humanitarian">humanitarian</a> values, as well as awareness towards men's issues.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-3 .toclevel-2 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-4 .toclevel-3 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-5 .toclevel-4 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-6 .toclevel-5 ul,.mw-parser-output .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Inaugurated in 1992 on 7 February by Thomas Oaster,<sup id="cite_ref-IMD-History-kansas-stream-1991-92_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD-History-kansas-stream-1991-92-4">[4]</a></sup> the project of International Men's Day was conceived one year earlier on 8 February 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The project was re-initialised in 1999 in Trinidad and Tobago.<sup id="cite_ref-Caribbean_Stream_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caribbean_Stream-6">[6]</a></sup> The longest running celebration of International Men's Day is <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, where events have occurred since 7 February 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Now as Malta was the only country that observed the February date of celebrating Men and their contribution to the society, the Maltese AMR Committee voted in 2009 to shift the date for IMD to 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Jerome Teelucksingh, who revived the event, chose 19 November to honour his father's birthday and also to celebrate how on that date in 1989 <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago's</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> team had united the country with their endeavours to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/1989_in_football_(soccer)" class="mw-redirect" title="1989 in football (soccer)">World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Teelucksingh has promoted International Men's Day as not just a gendered day but a day where all issues affecting men and boys can be addressed. He has said of IMD and its grass roots activists, "They are striving for <a href="/wiki/Gender_equality" title="Gender equality">gender equality</a> and patiently attempt to remove the negative images and the stigma associated with men in our society".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Yearly_themes">Yearly themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Yearly themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>As well as the six Core Objectives, an optional secondary theme for IMD has usually been suggested by world coordinators, such as peace in 2002, men's health in 2003, healing and forgiveness in 2007, positive male role models in 2009 and 'our children's future' in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-International_Men's_Day'_p.11_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International_Men's_Day'_p.11-13">[13]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2011_.22Giving_Boys_the_Best_Possible_Start_in_Life.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011_&quot;Giving_Boys_the_Best_Possible_Start_in_Life&quot;">2011 "Giving Boys the Best Possible Start in Life"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2011 &quot;Giving Boys the Best Possible Start in Life&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2011, the theme for international Men's Day is 'boys' with the title, "Giving Boys the Best Possible Start in Life".<sup id="cite_ref-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD-12">[12]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2012_.22Helping_Men_and_Boys_Live_Longer.2C_Happier_and_Healthier_Lives.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_&quot;Helping_Men_and_Boys_Live_Longer,_Happier_and_Healthier_Lives&quot;">2012 "Helping Men and Boys Live Longer, Happier and Healthier Lives"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2012 &quot;Helping Men and Boys Live Longer, Happier and Healthier Lives&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The theme for 2012 was 'health' with the title "Helping Men and Boys Live Longer, Happier and Healthier Lives".<sup id="cite_ref-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD_Global_Website_-_About_IMD-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2013_.22Keeping_Men_and_Boys_Safe.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013_&quot;Keeping_Men_and_Boys_Safe&quot;">2013 "Keeping Men and Boys Safe"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2013 &quot;Keeping Men and Boys Safe&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The theme for 2013 as nominated by the IMD Coordination Committee is, "Keeping Men and Boys Safe". The 2013 Press Release asks, "People all over the world are used to relating to men as protectors and providers, but how often do we consider the actions we can all take to protect Men and Boys from harm and provide them with a safe world where they can thrive and prosper?"<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2014_.22Working_Together_for_Men_and_Boys.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_&quot;Working_Together_for_Men_and_Boys&quot;">2014 "Working Together for Men and Boys"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014 &quot;Working Together for Men and Boys&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>2014 International Men's Day theme was "Working Together for Men and Boys".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2015_.22Working_to_Expand_Reproductive_Options_for_Men.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015_&quot;Working_to_Expand_Reproductive_Options_for_Men&quot;">2015 "Working to Expand Reproductive Options for Men"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2015 &quot;Working to Expand Reproductive Options for Men&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The International Men's Day theme for 2015 was "Working to Expand Reproductive Options for Men".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2016_.22Stop_Male_Suicide.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016_&quot;Stop_Male_Suicide&quot;">2016 "Stop Male Suicide"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2016 &quot;Stop Male Suicide&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>2016's theme for International Men's Day was "Stop Male Suicide". In every country except <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate" title="List of countries by suicide rate">rate of suicide</a> in men is higher than that of women, in some cases as high as six men for every one woman, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">life expectancy</a> is routinely less for men than women in all countries. To this end, "Global Action on Mens Health (GAMH) wants the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> and other international public health bodies, as well as individual governments, to acknowledge the scale of the problems facing men and boys and to take sustained action to tackle them. This work should sit alongside continuing action to improve the health of women and girls."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Glen Poole, an IMD coordinator wrote a book entitled "How You Can Stop Male Suicide in 7 Simple Steps", summarized with the motto "Learn, love, listen".<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2017_.22Celebrating_Men_And_Boys_In_All_Their_Diversity.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_&quot;Celebrating_Men_And_Boys_In_All_Their_Diversity&quot;">2017 "Celebrating Men And Boys In All Their Diversity"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2017 &quot;Celebrating Men And Boys In All Their Diversity&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In March 2017, the theme of "Celebrating Men And Boys In All Their Diversity" was announced by the Global and Regional Coordinators.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> The emphasis on "...A&nbsp;Call To Action for individuals, institutions, and organizations to innovate the manner in which they design and deliver resources and support services which speak to the unique needs and issues of men and boys".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2018_.22Positive_Male_Role_Models.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_&quot;Positive_Male_Role_Models&quot;">2018 "Positive Male Role Models"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2018 &quot;Positive Male Role Models&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The theme of 2018's International Men's Day was "Positive Male Role Models", and focused on giving men and boys good positive role models to look up to.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2019_.22Making_a_Difference_for_Men_and_Boys.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2019_&quot;Making_a_Difference_for_Men_and_Boys&quot;">2019 "Making a Difference for Men and Boys"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2019 &quot;Making a Difference for Men and Boys&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The theme of 2019's International Men's Day was "Making a Difference for Men and Boys," and focused on promoting the need to value men and boys and help people make practical improvements in men and boy's health and well-being.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="2020_.22Better_Health_for_Men_and_Boys.22"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020_&quot;Better_Health_for_Men_and_Boys&quot;">2020 "Better Health for Men and Boys"</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2020 &quot;Better Health for Men and Boys&quot;">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The 2020 theme is "Better Health for Men and Boys" with the aim to make practical improvements to the health and wellbeing of the male population.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History_2">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_background">Early background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Early background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Calls for an International Men's Day have been noted since at least the 1960s, when many men were reported to "have been agitating privately to make 23 February International Men's Day, the equivalent of 8 March, which is International Women's Day"<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> this day was The <a href="/wiki/Defender_of_the_Fatherland_Day" title="Defender of the Fatherland Day">Red Army and Navy Day</a> since 1922, which in 2002 was renamed to <a href="/wiki/Defender_of_the_Fatherland_Day" title="Defender of the Fatherland Day">Defender of the Fatherland Day</a>. The date was informally viewed a male counterpart of Women's Day (8 March) in some territories of the Union, however due to the day's limited focus to historical events some countries of the former union have moved to adopt the more 'male specific' 19 November as International Men's Day, including <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1968 the American journalist John P. Harris wrote an editorial in the <a href="/wiki/The_Salina_Journal" title="The Salina Journal">Salina Journal</a> highlighting a lack of balance in the Soviet system, which promoted an International Women's Day for the female workers without promoting a corresponding day for male workers. Harris stated that although he did not begrudge Soviet women their March day of glory, its resulting gender inequality clearly exhibited a serious flaw in the <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> system, which, "makes much of the equal rights it has given the sexes, but as it turns out, the women are much more equal than the men".<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-26">[26]</a></sup> Harris stated that while the men toiled along in their grooves doing what their government and womenfolk tell them to do, there was no day when males are recognised for their service, leading Harris to conclude that "This strikes me as unwarranted discrimination and rank injustice".<sup id="cite_ref-Harris_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris-26">[26]</a></sup> Similar questions about the inequality of observing women's day without a corresponding men's day occurred in media publications from the 1960s through to the 1990s,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-imd11_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imd11-28">[28]</a></sup> at which time the first attempts at inaugurating international Men's Day are recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the early 1990s, organizations in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> held small events in February at the invitation of Thomas Oaster who directed the Missouri Center for Men's Studies at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Missouri%E2%80%93Kansas_City" title="University of MissouriKansas City">University of MissouriKansas City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMD-History-kansas-stream-1991-92_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMD-History-kansas-stream-1991-92-4">[4]</a></sup> Oaster successfully promoted the event in 1993 and 1994, but his following attempt in 1995 was poorly attended and he ceased plans to continue the event in subsequent years.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Australians also ceased to observe the event (until they re-established it on 19 November 2003) whilst the Maltese Association for Men's Rights continued as the only country that continued to observe the event each year in February.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> Formerly being the only country still observing the original February date, the Maltese AMR Committee voted in 2009 to begin observing the day on 19 November in order to be synchronized with the rest of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Caribbean_Stream_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caribbean_Stream-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although International Men's and Women's Day are considered to be 'gender focused' events, they are not ideological mirror images because they highlight issues that are considered unique to men or to women.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> The history of IMD primarily concerns celebrating issues that are considered unique to the experiences of men and boys, along with an emphasis on positive role models, which is especially "deemed necessary in a social context which is often fascinated with images of males behaving badly... In highlighting positive male role models IMD attempts to show that males of all ages respond much more energetically to positive role models than they do to negative stereotyping."<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trinidad_and_Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Trinidad and Tobago">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Citizens in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> were the first to observe IMD on 19 November 1999. The event was conceived and coordinated by Dr. Jerome Teelucksingh from The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_West_Indies" title="University of the West Indies">University of the West Indies</a> at the Families in Action headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Newtown,_Port_of_Spain" title="Newtown, Port of Spain">Newtown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>. As his rationale for creating the event Dr. Teelucksingh stated, "I realized there was no day for men... some have said that there is <a href="/wiki/Father%27s_Day" title="Father's Day">Father's Day</a>, but what about young boys, teenagers and men who are not fathers?"<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> Dr. Teelucksingh, understanding the importance of celebrating good male role models, felt that his own father had been an example of an excellent role model and so chose 19 November partly because this was his father's birthday, and also because it was the date on which a local sporting team in his country created a level of unity with transcended gender, religious and ethnic divisions.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The idea of celebrating an International Men's Day received written support from officials in <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> and the event has continued to be celebrated annually in Trinidad and Tobago and other countries since its beginning.<sup id="cite_ref-Caribbean_Stream_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Caribbean_Stream-6">[6]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jamaica">Jamaica</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Jamaica">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Jamaicans" title="Jamaicans">Jamaicans</a> held an inaugural IMD observation on 19 November 2001, with a church service at Northgate Family Church in <a href="/wiki/Ocho_Rios" title="Ocho Rios">Ocho Rios</a>, an educational session with male students at Ferncourt High School, and public forum at Brown's Town Community College. Keynote speaker at the event was Luciano who talked on the theme of 'Today's Man, Tomorrow's Future'. A special theme of the event was discussions on <i>men's sexual health and reproduction</i>. Nurse Bunnaman of the Beth Jacobs Family Planning Clinic in St. Ann's Bay told <a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Star_(Jamaica)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Star (Jamaica) (page does not exist)">The Star</a> Newspaper "This is the first time that Jamaica will be observing International Men's Day. It was started in Trinidad in 1999. This year it will be observed in Kenya, Tanzania, Norway, Brazil, Germany, Britain and the United States of America as well".<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Educational sessions about men's <a href="/wiki/Reproductive_health" title="Reproductive health">sexual health</a> and reproduction were held by the Beth Jacobs Clinic, where medical check-ups and testicular checks were given free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Australia">Australia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Australia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Australians have celebrated IMD on 19 November since 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> when Phil Gouldson of Men's Health and Wellbeing Association ACT (MHWA) launched the inaugural event after receiving an invitation by Trinidad and Tobago's Harrack Balramsingh to join in the event.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> In Canberra, 2004, Gouldson asked men in Australia to wear a red rose for IMD and for women and families to buy the men in their life flowers. He said a red rose is worn by men on IMD as a symbol of strength of character and courage, and as it is unusual to see men being given flowers so it is a good way to highlight the occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Flood" title="Michael Flood">Michael Flood</a>, an academic, criticized the basis of the 'Men's Health and Wellbeing Association' (MHWA)'s IMD celebration which focused on men's health, arguing that there were already enough opportunities to work on men's health and fatherhood (citing Father's Day and Men's Health Week).<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Gouldson responded, reminding that "Not all men and boys are fathers, while Men's Health Week focuses on claimed inadequacies of men in not better managing their health".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Teelucksingh independently highlighted the need to address the needs of young boys, teenagers and men who are not fathers, which was one of his primary purposes for establishing International Men's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008 Dads4Kids Organization highlighted the theme 'honour and sacrifice', pointing to the sinking of the cruiser <a href="/wiki/HMAS_Sydney_(1934)" class="mw-redirect" title="HMAS Sydney (1934)">HMAS <i>Sydney</i></a> on 19 November during the Second World War which resulted in the death of 645 men off the coast of Geraldton in Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-Dads4Kids_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dads4Kids-41">[41]</a></sup> Organisers said, "men make sacrifices every day in their place of work, in their role as husbands and fathers, for their families, for their friends, for their communities and for their nation".<sup id="cite_ref-Dads4Kids_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dads4Kids-41">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009, a number of events were held throughout Australia including IMD initiatives organized by four local governments: <a href="/wiki/Maitland_City_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Maitland City Council">Maitland City Council</a> in N.S.W., <a href="/wiki/Greater_Hume_Shire_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Greater Hume Shire Council">Greater Hume Shire Council</a> in Victoria, <a href="/wiki/Ipswich_City_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Ipswich City Council">Ipswich City Council</a> in Queensland, and <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Shire_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Forbes Shire Council">Forbes Shire Council</a> in N.S.W. each of whom funded local observations. These were the first government bodies in Australia to fund and host community IMD events.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In the State <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Western_Australia" title="Parliament of Western Australia">Parliament of Western Australia</a> Minister <a href="/wiki/Nick_Goiran" title="Nick Goiran">Nick Goiran</a> gave a speech introducing International Men's Day and its objectives to the parliament, focussing on the promotion of gender equality and the importance of highlighting positive male role models.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> There was also an event held in the Federal <a href="/wiki/Australian_Parliament_House" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Parliament House">Australian Parliament House</a> with several notable speakers.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> Numerous other organisations hosted observations including the Men's Shed Steering Committee in <a href="/wiki/Rockhampton,_Queensland" class="mw-redirect" title="Rockhampton, Queensland">Rockhampton</a>, the Community Resource center in <a href="/wiki/Ulladulla" class="mw-redirect" title="Ulladulla">Ulladulla</a>, the Regional Health Service in Koo Wee Rup, and <i>Dads on the Air</i> radio programme in Sydney which hosted an hour-long programme discussing IMD with a panel of international coordinators of the event.<sup id="cite_ref-Dads4Kids_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dads4Kids-41">[41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In honour of men and boys on the occasion of IMD 2014, Liz Behjat addressed the Western Australian Legislative Council on the topic of men's lives and issues.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="India">India</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: India">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The inaugural celebration of IMD in India was organized by the leading Indian Men's rights organization Indian Family on 19 November 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> The date of 19 November was accepted based on the fact that Australia and the West Indies (Jamaica, Trinidad and Tobago) were already observing IMD on that date. The event was again celebrated in India in 2008, and plans were made to continue the celebration annually.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:294px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg/292px-Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg" decoding="async" width="292" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg/438px-Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg/584px-Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1032" data-file-height="774"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Avijan_is_protesting_for_Men_Right_in_Kolkata.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Men's Rights Demonstrations in India.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2009, India received the first corporate sponsorship of the International Men's Day with menswear brand Allen Solly deciding to create promotional offers on IMD, and <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> deciding to screen male-positive movies in its "Men in Black" series on 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> In 2014, Confidare Education Consultancy hosted an International Men's Day <a href="/wiki/Art_gallery" title="Art gallery">art gallery</a> in New Delhi,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> while in Kolkata protests were held to highlight men's rights and abuse of the elderly.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Other <a href="/wiki/Men%27s_rights" class="mw-redirect" title="Men's rights">men's rights</a> activists posed questions on the occasion of IMD, questioning the lack of gender neutrality in laws about domestic violence and child custody.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> The Chennai chapter of All India Men's Welfare Association (AIMWA) submitted a memorandum to the government on IMD 2014, demanding the establishment of a Men's Welfare Ministry, National Commission for Men, and making all laws gender neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2018, Avijan, a welfare and charitable trust for men, organized a protest in Kolkata to demand gender neutrality in law, a men's commission in India, repealing of <a href="/wiki/Section_498A" class="mw-redirect" title="Section 498A">Section 498A</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Penal_Code" title="Indian Penal Code">Indian Penal Code</a>, and strong action against misuse of the rape law.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Save_Indian_Family_Foundation" title="Save Indian Family Foundation">Save Indian Family</a>  Karnataka (SIF Karnataka), an NGO working for Men's Rights in India under Save Indian Family Movement, celebrates International Men's Day every year. In 2019, in association with two major hospitals of Bangalore, Aster Hospitals and Regal Hospital, it ran a #HealthyHim campaign on prostate cancer awareness.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> In 2017 and 2018, among many other awareness activities, the volunteers organized a bike rally to <a href="/wiki/Nandi_Hills,_India" title="Nandi Hills, India">Nandi Hills, India</a> and celebrated International Men's Day with more than 40,000 people present. </p>
      <p>Daaman Welfare Society &amp; Trust, another prominent NGO working on the same principals under the Save Indian Family Movement, also celebrates International Men's Day every year. In 2019, it hosted a day long grand event at Rave 3 Mall in Kanpur and created awareness on International Men's Day. The need for National Men's Commission was also discussed.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="China">China</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2003, a fashion magazine proposed 3 August as the International Men's day, corresponding to the International Women's day held on 8 March. The magazine claimed to have submitted a proposal to UNESCO. Ever since then, the topic about "Men's Day" has been discussed every August on the Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note--62">[62]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Hong Kong in 2010 special observances of International Men's Day occurred on 19 November, with the theme "Blessed Are The Men". All men were invited to ride for free in the city's Ngong Ping 360 Tung Chung cable cars for a round-trip on 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-China_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-63">[63]</a></sup> In the same year an article in <i>China Daily</i> on 3 August asked whether men in China needed their own special day, citing the fact that on International Women's Day all women in China, who accounted for 45 percent of the workforce, get a mandatory half day off by their employer while men had no such day. The article reported on an online survey done by Shanghai Hotline asking "Do men need a holiday for themselves?"  to which 80.24 percent of respondents said "yes" with many insisting that Shanghai men are tired and deserve a holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-China_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-China-63">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">United States</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: United States">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The following states and cities have recognized International Men's Day: <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a>, New York, <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a> (Luther College in <a href="/wiki/Decorah,_Iowa" title="Decorah, Iowa">Decorah</a>, Iowa), <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">Alabama</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">Michigan</a>; <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C</a>.; <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>; <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>2012 International Men's Day was celebrated during the weeks before the observance of 2012 International Men's Day on 12 October 2012. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2014, over 25 organisations held events across the UK  including two in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a>. This was continued in 2015 where <a href="/wiki/Philip_Davies" title="Philip Davies">Philip Davies</a> MP introduced a debate in the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Westminster" title="Palace of Westminster">Palace of Westminster</a> about men's issues on 19 November.<sup id="cite_ref-debate2015_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-debate2015-65">[65]</a></sup> and the Day has been endorsed by the Prime Minister, <a href="/wiki/Theresa_May" title="Theresa May">Theresa May</a>. In 2016, over 60 events were held.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> 2018 was the biggest International Men's Day to date in the UK with more than 200 events, campaigns and celebrations held.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In 2019 the themes encouraged people and organised to "Make A Difference" and "Give men and boys better life chances" and again, over 200 events took place.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="England">England</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: England">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In England (and the UK) the event was inaugurated in 2008 by <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kent" title="University of Kent">University of Kent</a> students who celebrated International Men's Day on the university campus on 19 November 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> This event was organized and coordinated by the Kent University student group 'The Bishopden Boys'. The Bishopden boy's were a Kent Union charitable group, located in Bishopden court, which raises money for various charities each year. Activities for IMD night included 7 a side football tournament, comedy acts and a live music festival, fronted by the student band "Jad". There was a raffle, a guitar hero competition and an <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a> tournament to raise money. All proceeds raised went to ORCHID a charity for all male cancers, including <a href="/wiki/Prostate" title="Prostate">prostate</a>, penile or testicular cancer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2010 the Brighton Men's Network organised an IMD conference event for the city of Brighton for professionals, experts and people interested in helping the city in improving services for men and boys. Chair of the Men's Network Glen Poole stated that public sector bosses, the voluntary sector, business leaders and concerned individuals will come together and explore how to help all men and boys live more fulfilled lives and make a bigger contribution to the city, and concluded, "This event will be an important step towards getting people to agree on the actions we need to take and help us develop the world's first citywide strategy for men and boys that we aim to launch next year."<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> At Hartlepool, Rossmere Youth Centre hosted an IMD evening for boys and girls between the ages of 13 and 19 focused on health, gender equality and promoting male role models. Activities included rides on a rodeo bull, a Gladiators-style event, an Indian head massage, and dressing up in sumo suits. Organisations Springboard, Nacro and Jobsmart attended to give information and advice on training opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> On 19 November 2010 Tiemo Entertainment sponsored a 'Celebration of Men Dinner' in London's Hotel Ibis in Euston, with Keynote Speaker Mr Damion Queva  Publisher of Fathers Quarterly magazine. Discussions were conducted on the topic, "What is the purpose of International Men's Day?" and attendees were treated to a wide-ranging discussion of some of the key issues facing men today. The mixed panel of professionals (including women) included Investment Analyst Michael Young, HR Manager Beverley Green, Builder and Reach Role Model Hylton Forrester, Wendy Forrester, Michael Peters, Polish Publisher Anna Prochon and the Keynote speaker Damion Queva, Publisher of Fathers Quarterly magazine in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Planned events to mark IMD at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_York" title="University of York">University of York</a> in 2015 were cancelled by the University, after pressure from about 200 members of staff, students, and alumni,<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian001_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian001-76">[76]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-independent001_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent001-77">[77]</a></sup> who signed an open letter on 13 November. The letter argued that "A day that celebrates mens issues... does not combat inequality, but merely amplifies existing, structurally imposed, inequalities", characterizing a statement from the university's equality and diversity committee in support of the event as "particularly crass in view of the fact that of the 12-strong university senior management group, three-quarters are male".<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian001_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian001-76">[76]</a></sup> Subsequently, the University made no plans to mark the event in 2016,<sup id="cite_ref-theyourker001_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theyourker001-78">[78]</a></sup> despite a counter-petition which attracted 4,261 supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian001_76-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian001-76">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Ireland">Northern Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Northern Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In Northern Ireland 2010 Deputy Mayor of Newry and Mourne Council, Cllr Karen Mc Kevitt launched the Magnet Young Men's Health Event,' on Friday 19 November. The event was attended by men from across the district and representatives from local statutory, voluntary and community organisations were organised to celebrate 19 November as International Men's Day. Deputy Mayor, Cllr Mc Kevitt said, It is a great idea to give an issue that has an international perspective a local focus. All men need to look after their health and take advantage of the services and help that is out there, as we all do. But it is particularly good to see an event that looks at the barriers that young men may be facing and brings together people from all organisations across the district to look at what can be done to work together to make things better.'<sup id="cite_ref-crossexaminer.co.uk_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossexaminer.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup> The event offered opportunities for men to have health checks with experienced staff from Action Cancer, and speakers such as Ken Harland (University of Ulster's Centre of Young Men's studies), Peter Mc Donald, a senior child care worker from Giggles Daycare nursery, and local athlete Ronan Murtagh shared their own insight into the choices young men make and the opportunities that are out there for young men today. Also in attendance was Jerome Burns, Assistant Director, Department for Social Development. Jerome stated, "The department for Social Development is delighted to support local initiatives that work with young men to highlight inequalities in health."<sup id="cite_ref-crossexaminer.co.uk_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crossexaminer.co.uk-79">[79]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Scotland">Scotland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Scotland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>IMD was inaugurated in Scotland in 2010. The event was endorsed by the Government of Scotland and by the Men's Health Forum of Scotland (MHFS).<sup id="cite_ref-scotland.gov.uk_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotland.gov.uk-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mhfs.org.uk_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mhfs.org.uk-81">[81]</a></sup> The MHFS celebrated the day with a roundtable event to promote the health and wellbeing of men and boys by bringing together key people and organisations. The focus of the event was to discuss the rationale for developing a national men's health policy in Scotland. The event took place at Elliot House, the office of <a href="/wiki/NHS_Quality_Improvement_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS Quality Improvement Scotland">NHS Quality Improvement Scotland</a> (QIS) in Edinburgh, where there were representations from Scottish Government, NHS Leads and Directors in the Voluntary Health Sector who discussed the issues and set up a short term task group to take this work forward. Jim Leishman, Men's Health Coordinator, NHS Forth Valley said: "This event was a huge opportunity to drive through improvements in men's health in Scotland."<sup id="cite_ref-scotland.gov.uk_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scotland.gov.uk-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mhfs.org.uk_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mhfs.org.uk-81">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Wales">Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In 2011 The Welsh Government was accused by Tory councillor Peter Davies (father of MP <a href="/wiki/Philip_Davies" title="Philip Davies">Philip Davies</a>) of sex discrimination for supporting International Women's Day with grants totalling 30,000 while ignoring International Men's Day. Davies stated, "I don't particularly object to the Welsh Government spending money on International Women's Day, but I would have thought that with its commitment to equality it would also be happy to recognise International Men's Day, which will be celebrated this Saturday."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singapore">Singapore</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Singapore">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2008, a 1921 November IMD event was organized in Singapore. The Adam Association organized a forum  Definition of a Man  which identified various problems men face at home such as communication issues, and how to overcome them. Held in <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a>, speakers included <a href="/wiki/Maliki_Osman" title="Maliki Osman">Maliki Osman</a>, Parliamentary Secretary for National Development, and staff members from the Registry of Marriages. The forum was open to the public for free and was held at the Darussalam mosque along Commonwealth Avenue West. Another event, also part of International Men's Day, was the Admiralty Baby Genius and Kids' Fashion contest, held on Sunday at Woodlands. Jointly organized by Adam Association and Ace the Place Community Club Management Committee, activities included a diaper-changing contest for fathers.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-70">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2009 the National Family Council launched the <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Dads_for_Life_movement" title="Singapore Dads for Life movement">Singapore Dads for Life movement</a> to support a man's role in co-parenting.<sup id="cite_ref-Aim_of_new_network_for_Dads_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aim_of_new_network_for_Dads-84">[84]</a></sup> As part of the event volunteers distributed men's 'toolkits' at more than 30 locations to mark International Men's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Another organization, the Father's Action Network (FAN) also handed out "Dads for Life" toolkits and asked people to share personal stories of fatherhood which were placed online.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">Romania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Romania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>As of 19 November 2016 Romania will officially celebrate the "national men's day". The law declaring 19 November as the national men's day was passed on 2 February 2016 by the Romanian parliament. Romania is the first country to officially recognize and celebrate this as a national day. National women's day is also held on 8 March.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Malta">Malta</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Malta">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>International Men's Day has been celebrated in Malta by the Association for Men's Rights since 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> AMR founder and director John Zammit conceived the event which has been held yearly in the form of a dinner, lunch or reception for AMR members and public. On this occasion awards are given to individuals who have made distinctive contributions men's rights such as, for example, efforts made by committee members, "for the removal of the impediment of departure which we had on men in separation/divorce cases. Before 1995 all men who had problems with their wives in Malta, be it Maltese or foreigners, could not leave the island while their case was still in court and so were imprisoned in Malta."<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The Malta event has traditionally been observed on 7 February since 1994, making it the longest running local IMD observation in the world. As the February date is not celebrated by other participating countries and did not qualify as an <i>internationally</i> observed date, discussions were undertaken within the Maltese Association for Men's Rights, and on 17 January 2009, the committee voted unanimously to shift their celebrations to 19 November to coincide with all the others around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Malta_&amp;_South_Africa_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malta_&amp;_South_Africa-90">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hungary">Hungary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Hungary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In November 2009, writer Marie Clarence organized the inaugural IMD celebration for Hungary. Clarence organized the event to promote gender balance and gender equity. The celebration was held in Budapest and the UNESCO Cultural Committee Chairman of Hungary Michael Hoppal gave the opening speech. The event included celebration of local culture, including dancing and forum discussions which highlighted men's achievements and contributions to the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa">South Africa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: South Africa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:139px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:GeorgeBushKgalemaMotlanthe_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bc/GeorgeBushKgalemaMotlanthe_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="137" height="175" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="137" data-file-height="175"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:GeorgeBushKgalemaMotlanthe_crop.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Deputy President <a href="/wiki/Kgalema_Motlanthe" title="Kgalema Motlanthe">Kgalema Motlanthe</a> addressed an International Men's Day gathering in South Africa 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Positive Men's Movement of South Africa (POMESA)<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> in partnership with South African Network of People Living with HIV and AIDS (NAPWA)<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> organized the first Annual International Men's Day event. The event was held on 6 December 2008, and involved a Men's March for peace and justice from taxi rank to the national men's rally venue which is Rabasotho hall in Thembisa township, Ekurhuleni, Gauteng. Between three and five thousand men attended from all provinces of South Africa. Speakers in the event included the national government officials, national leadership of POMESA and NAPWA, and civil society, and included an Annual Men's Awards event to honour three outstanding men who have or and continue to contribute positively in the creation of peaceful and just society.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mensday.org.za_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensday.org.za-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, POMESA and NAPWA celebrated IMD on 6 December.<sup id="cite_ref-mensday.org.za_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensday.org.za-93">[93]</a></sup> As the December date was not celebrated by other participating countries, discussions were undertaken within both organizations and in May 2009 the Secretary General of NAPWA and POMESA Nkululeko Nxesi announced that the National Boards of both organizations have agreed to celebrate the Men's day on the same dates with other countries beginning on 19 November 2009 and in each year thereafter on the same date.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Malta_&amp;_South_Africa_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malta_&amp;_South_Africa-90">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 November 2009 five thousand men from across Africa converged on the Orlando Communal Hall in Soweto to celebrate the second annual International Men's Day, where they promoted gender equality, positive male role models and emphasised that not all men are bad people'.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Deputy President of South Africa Kgalema Motlanthe delivered the keynote address at what was termed "a ground-breaking event". The meeting was organized and led by the National Association of People Living With HIV and AIDS (NAPWA) to highlight the need for treatment access to medication and prevention.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ghana">Ghana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ghana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Ghana Fatherhood Initiative Foundation hosted an inaugural IMD celebration in 2009. The occasion was marked by a formal event with speakers, and included a ceremony of donating of books to several schools in the Ablekuma sub-district in Accra. The event was chaired by George Odame, the advisory board chairman of Ghana Fatherhood Initiative Foundation, who encouraged all fathers to read to their children as part of responsible fatherhood. The special guest of honour was Maxwell Mac. Ocloo who delivered a speech entitled 'Men  let us be instruments of positive influence' in which he encouraged men to lead by example.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tanzania">Tanzania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tanzania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On Saturday 19 November 2011, Youth Challenge International (YCI), in partnership with local and international organizations celebrated International Men's Day for the first time in <a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morogoro" title="Morogoro">Morogoro</a>, Tanzania. In Arusha, YCI, The Umoja Centre, Support for International Change, UMATI, Initiative for Youth Organization and Global Service Corps hosted the event at the Mbauda Open Market Ground. This event was aimed to promote men and boys as positive role models and to educate the community on the role of males and females in health, education, family life, violence and life choices. The event included performances, games, and educational activities. Over 500 youth and other community members came together to acknowledge the roles and responsibilities of men and boys in creating a brighter future for all Tanzanians. To celebrate the event in Morogoro, volunteers, along with partner organization Faraja Trust Fund, held a soccer tournament on with 8 local teams. To qualify to participate in the tournament each team had to come to two information sessions on male sexual and reproductive health, HIV/AIDS, gender roles and good governance. YCI and Faraja provided an on-site HIV testing centre, a DJ with music and dancing throughout the day, and drama group performances on the key objectives of International Men's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Plans exist for the Tanzanian Men's Rights Organisation (TAMRA) to celebrate International men's day in 2013. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Zimbabwe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>International Men's Day was inaugurated in Zimbabwe on 19 November 2011. The commemorations were held at Chibuku Stadium in Chitungwiza under the theme Giving The Boy Child The Best Possible Start In Life. Fred Misi, the chairman of Men's Forum Varume Svinurai/Vhukhani said the commemorations came at a time when attention was being given to the girl child at the expense of boys, and noted, "Whilst it is important to focus on the specific needs of the girl child, we are creating a crisis by ignoring the specific needs of the boy child," Misi highlighted the growing trend that many boys were dropping out of school and were hooked on hard drugs as well as abusing alcohol, while a significant number of those who were completed secondary and tertiary education were roaming the streets because of unemployment. He added the government and Zimbabweans needed to act immediately. A number of prominent persons attended and gave papers on the need to give the boy child assistance. There was drama and poetry from various groups and individual high school students in line with the theme of the celebrations, and the Zimbabwe Minister of Women Affairs, Gender and Community Development, Olivia Muchena gave a key note address in which she said, "It is an occasion for men to celebrate their achievements and contributions, in particular their contributions to community, family, marriage and child care while highlighting the discrimination against them... International Men's Day is an opportunity for people everywhere of good will to appreciate and celebrate the men in their life and the contributions they make to society for the greater good of all hence it being important for us to celebrate this day equally as we did with The International Women's Day."<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botswana">Botswana</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Botswana">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>International Men's Day was inaugurated in Botswana in 2011 by coordinator Geneuvieve Twala. One of the International Men's Day themes promoted was to help foster youth to unlock their creative identities to allow them to share their gifts with peers, family and the community, and to be seen and heard for who they are and not how they are perceived. The primary event was a gala dinner titled "One moment for Change" to highlight men's potential and the increasing capabilities of men as innovators of society. The dinner was held to raise funds to cover six months music tuition fees for a group of 20 children from the SOS Children's Village whom IMD ambassadors have adopted as part of a mentoring programme for children. Standard Chartered Bank sponsored the dinner, which included a range of iconic speakers who shared their experience and insights with the audience. Standard Chartered Bank Acting CEO Mr Michael Wiegand opened the event by sharing best practices that Standard Chartered Bank uses to address legitimate issues faced by male employees, including the fact that Standard Chartered Bank is the first company in Botswana to offer paternity leave which, he stated, made their male employees feel valued and that they were working for a 21st-century organization. Mr Tebogo Sebego, senior partner at Sebego &amp; Sharma Attorneys and former chairperson of the Law Society of Botswana gave a keynote speech where he emphasized how the child protection laws should be improved, how the society play a role in creating a safe environment for the future generation of men. Mrs Tjipo Mothobi, Director, GBC Health South Africa gave an address on business collective effort. The District Commissioner in his closing remarks made an announcement that by end of December he was convening a meeting with men in the City where they will engage in dialogue on how they can collectively address the issues and challenges men and boys face. The inaugural event was a success, with radio stations subsequently airing programmes that call for debate on men's issues since IMD. All the businesses and stakeholders involved gave a commitment to be part and parcel of the next IMD and we are already working on the strategy for 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Seychelles">Seychelles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Seychelles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 19 November 2012 Government Minister <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Meriton" title="Vincent Meriton">Vincent Meriton</a> declared this year the first that IMD has been celebrated at a National Government level. Minister Meriton said, "The time has come for us to adopt a new approach, instead of reinforcing negative stereotyping of males behaving badly, e.g. media portrayals of males as violent, power-hungry, irresponsible and so on. Such negative images are frequently used in an attempt to shame males into behaving more positively."<sup id="cite_ref-nation.sc_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nation.sc-102">[102]</a></sup> Meriton stated that the practice of negative stereotyping ignores the fact that such negative behaviours do not apply to the vast majority of men and boys, or that such negativity may detrimentally impact the self-image and self-esteem of boys, which in turn impacts their willingness to contribute to building better relationships and communities as they grow into adults. In conclusion he stated that "International Men's Day calls for and promotes positive masculinity which we in Seychelles can strongly identify with as it forms part of the social renaissance campaign launched at the beginning of the year by President James Michel."<sup id="cite_ref-nation.sc_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nation.sc-102">[102]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Burundi">Burundi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Burundi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 19 November 2012 Burundi joined the world for the first time in celebrating the International Men's Day, as Association for the Protection of the Man in Distress (APHD Burundi) denounced violence inflicted to men by their wives. Vincent Bukuru, chairman of the APHD-Burundi said, "Violence on men rises when the man loses his job, during the end of year festivities (Christmas and New Year) and at the <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">International Women's Day</a> (8 March)."<sup id="cite_ref-newtimes.co.rw_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newtimes.co.rw-103">[103]</a></sup> Bukuru called on the Burundian government to conduct a national investigation on types and origins of violence that men are facing, their consequences and their gravity which he stated is a violation of human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-newtimes.co.rw_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newtimes.co.rw-103">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ireland">Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>To Celebrate International Men's Day on Thursday 19 November 2009, Irish broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Newstalk" title="Newstalk">Newstalk</a> devoted a day-long show to men. The show was hosted by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Dunne" title="Tom Dunne">Tom Dunne</a> and was Ireland's first ever observation of the event. Topics included discussion of how 'Men Sheds' contribute to improving men's health, and of their popularity in Ireland.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> In 2011 Men in Childcare Network Ireland and Men in Childcare Europe, a European network made up of Men in Childcare networks from individual EU member countries, hosted a European conference on "Reimagining Childhood Care &amp; Education" A celebration of Universal Children's Day, and International Men's Day. The event called 'Reimagining Childhood Care and Education' took place in Ireland on Saturday 19 November 2011 at the City West Hotel, Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup> Also in 2011 the Raphoe Family Resource Centre hosted an event with different groups in order to focus on the value of, and highlighting the positive contribution that men make. Children were invited to offer poems or stories about their fathers, grandfathers, uncles or big brothers which were put on display all week to show the men in families how important they are to others. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Isle_of_Man">Isle of Man</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Isle of Man">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Isle of Man celebrated its inaugural celebration in 2012 at the Isle of Man College of Higher education on 19 November 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-iomcollege.ac.im_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iomcollege.ac.im-105">[105]</a></sup> The organization emphasised the 2012 theme which highlighted World Health Organization figures showing that every year over half a million people die from violence and 83% of them are men and boys, and that a similar proportion of the <a href="/wiki/Disease_burden" title="Disease burden">global burden of disease</a> (ill-health, disability or early death) from violence is borne by males. For activities the NSC held strength tests and health advice; The Children's Centre loaned out their interactive babies and some parenting information and Will Sutton attended as the 'Positive' male role model for the day. The Student Council baked and sold cakes, and Sami-Jaine Martin (Student President) was running a Sexual Health Stand. The engineering group was selling moustaches and raising money for men's cancer charities, while construction group (with help from the art department) made an 8&nbsp;ft seaside cut out for photographs on the day. The beauty therapy department offered their time to pamper the boys with Indian head massages and face mapping, and there were also 3 students who volunteered to have their chest waxed to raise money for charity.<sup id="cite_ref-iomcollege.ac.im_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iomcollege.ac.im-105">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 19 November 2014 a total of 110 men took part in the all-male class led by Dave Smythe at the National Sports Centre in Douglas, which set the new world record for the Largest male yoga class, according to the World Record Academy. The event was the organized by Kate Bergquist, health and well-being co-ordinator at Isle of Man College to mark International Men's Day.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canada">Canada</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Men%27s_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Canada">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 19 November 2009, directors of the Vancouver Manology Program held an all day event to mark the beginning of the Vancouver Men's Centre. As a feature of this event organizers announced their official endorsement of International Men's Day and held forums introducing attendees to the history, goals and values of the international event, including discussions toward planning larger IMD events in 2010. This marks the first Canadian 19 Nov IMD observation.<sup id="cite_ref-Thompson_3-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thompson-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2010 Canada IMD Coordinator David Hatfield organized a large event at the Roundhouse in Vancouver for numerous male and family-friendly organizations to display their social work to the general public.
